       misconduct
      </a>
      by a caution (
      <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card" title="Penalty card">
       yellow card
      </a>
      ) or dismissal (
      <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card" title="Penalty card">
       red card
      </a>
      ). A second yellow card at the same game leads to a red card, and therefore to a dismissal. A player given a yellow card is said to have been "booked", the referee writing the player's name in his official notebook. If a player has been dismissed, no substitute can be brought on in their place. Misconduct may occur at any time, and while the offences that constitute misconduct are listed, the definitions are broad. In particular, the offence of "unsporting behaviour" may be used to deal with most events that violate the spirit of the game, even if they are not listed as specific offences. A referee can show a yellow or red card to a player, substitute or substituted player. Non-players such as managers and support staff cannot be shown the yellow or red card, but may be expelled from the technical area if they fail to conduct themselves in a responsible manner.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fouls_47-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-fouls-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Rather than stopping play, the referee may allow play to continue if doing so will benefit the team against which an offence has been committed. This is known as "playing an advantage".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The referee may "call back" play and penalise the original offence if the anticipated advantage does not ensue within "a few seconds". Even if an offence is not penalised due to advantage being played, the offender may still be sanctioned for misconduct at the next stoppage of play.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The referee's decision in all on-pitch matters is considered final.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The score of a match cannot be altered after the game, even if later evidence shows that decisions (including awards/non-awards of goals) were incorrect.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Off-field">
       Off-field
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foul_(association_football)#Post-match" title="Foul (association football)">
       Foul (association football)  Post-match
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Along with the general administration of the sport, football associations and competition organisers also enforce good conduct in wider aspects of the game, dealing with issues such as comments to the press, clubs' financial management,
      <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_sport" title="Doping in sport">
       doping
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Age_fraud_in_association_football" title="Age fraud in association football">
       age fraud
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">
       match fixing
      </a>
      . Most competitions enforce mandatory suspensions for players who are sent off in a game.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAsuspensions_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FAsuspensions-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some on-field incidents, if considered very serious (such as allegations of racial abuse), may result in competitions deciding to impose heavier sanctions than those normally associated with a red card.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some associations allow for appeals against player suspensions incurred on-field if clubs feel a referee was incorrect or unduly harsh.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAsuspensions_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FAsuspensions-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Sanctions for such infractions may be levied on individuals or on to clubs as a whole. Penalties may include fines, points deductions (in league competitions) or even expulsion from competitions. For example, the English and Scottish leagues will often deduct 10 points from a team that enters
      <a href="/wiki/Administration_(British_football)" title="Administration (British football)">
       financial administration
      </a>
      . Among other administrative sanctions are penalties against game forfeiture. Teams that had forfeited a game or had been forfeited against would be awarded a technical loss or win.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Governing_bodies">
       Governing bodies
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_around_the_world" title="Association football around the world">
       Association football around the world
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIFA-Headquarter.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="1701" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/FIFA-Headquarter.jpg/220px-FIFA-Headquarter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/FIFA-Headquarter.jpg/330px-FIFA-Headquarter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/FIFA-Headquarter.jpg/440px-FIFA-Headquarter.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FIFA-Headquarter.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Headquarters of
        <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
         FIFA
        </a>
        , the world governing body of football
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The recognised international governing body of football (and associated games, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">
       futsal
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">
       beach soccer
      </a>
      ) is
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
       FIFA
      </a>
      . The FIFA headquarters are located in
      <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zrich">
       Zrich
      </a>
      , Switzerland. Six regional confederations are associated with FIFA; these are:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confeds_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-confeds-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Asia:
       <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">
        Asian Football Confederation
       </a>
       (AFC)
      </li>
      <li>
       Africa:
       <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">
        Confederation of African Football
       </a>
       (CAF)
      </li>
      <li>
       Europe:
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">
        Union of European Football Associations
       </a>
       (UEFA)
      </li>
      <li>
       North/Central America &amp; Caribbean:
       <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">
        Confederation of North, Central American and Caribbean Association Football
       </a>
       (CONCACAF)
      </li>
      <li>
       Oceania:
       <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">
        Oceania Football Confederation
       </a>
       (OFC)
      </li>
      <li>
       South America:
       <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">
        Confederacin Sudamericana de Ftbol/Confederao Sul-americana de Futebol
       </a>
       (South American Football Confederation; CONMEBOL)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      National associations oversee football within individual countries. These are generally synonymous with sovereign states, (for example: the
      <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Camerounaise_de_Football" title="Fdration Camerounaise de Football">
       Fdration Camerounaise de Football
      </a>
      in Cameroon) but also include a smaller number of associations responsible for sub-national entities or autonomous regions (for example the
      <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">
       Scottish Football Association
      </a>
      in Scotland). 209 national associations are affiliated both with FIFA and with their respective continental confederations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confeds_86-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-confeds-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While FIFA is responsible for arranging competitions and most rules related to international competition, the actual Laws of the Game are set by the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Football_Association_Board" title="International Football Association Board">
       International Football Association Board
      </a>
      , where each of the UK Associations has one vote, while FIFA collectively has four votes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFAB_works_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-IFAB_works-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="International_competitions">
       International competitions
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_association_football_competitions" title="List of association football competitions">
       List of association football competitions
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1482" data-file-width="2106" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg/220px-Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg/330px-Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg/440px-Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mecz_Polska_-_Armenia_04_ssj_20070328.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_silence" title="Moment of silence">
         minute's silence
        </a>
        before an international match
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The major international competition in football is the
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
       World Cup
      </a>
      , organised by FIFA. This competition takes place every four years. Approximately 190200 national teams compete in qualifying tournaments within the scope of continental confederations for a place in the finals. The finals tournament, which is held every four years, involves 32 national teams competing over a four-week period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The most recent edition of the tournament was the
      <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">
       2014 FIFA World Cup
      </a>
      in Brazil.
     </p>
     <p>
      There has been a
      <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the Summer Olympics">
       football tournament
      </a>
      at every Summer Olympic Games since 1900, except at the 1932 games in
      <a href="/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics" title="1932 Summer Olympics">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Before the inception of the World Cup, the Olympics (especially during the 1920s) had the same status as the World Cup. Originally, the event was for amateurs only;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wherebegan_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wherebegan-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      however, since the
      <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">
       1984 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      , professional players have been permitted, albeit with certain restrictions which prevent countries from fielding their strongest sides. The Olympic men's tournament is played at Under-23 level. In the past the Olympics have allowed a restricted number of over-age players per team.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A women's tournament was added in 1996; in contrast to the men's event, full international sides without age restrictions play the women's Olympic tournament.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torres,_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="656" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg/220px-Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg/330px-Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg/440px-Torres%2C_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torres,_Mata_and_Ramos_Euro_2012_trophy_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Spanish footballers celebrating winning the
        <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">
         UEFA European Championship
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After the World Cup, the most important international football competitions are the continental championships, which are organised by each continental confederation and contested between national teams. These are the
      <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">
       European Championship
      </a>
      (UEFA), the
      <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Copa Amrica">
       Copa Amrica
      </a>
      (CONMEBOL),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" title="African Cup of Nations">
       African Cup of Nations
      </a>
      (CAF), the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Cup" title="Asian Cup">
       Asian Cup
      </a>
      (AFC), the
      <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">
       CONCACAF Gold Cup
      </a>
      (CONCACAF) and the
      <a href="/wiki/OFC_Nations_Cup" title="OFC Nations Cup">
       OFC Nations Cup
      </a>
      (OFC). The
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="FIFA Confederations Cup">
       FIFA Confederations Cup
      </a>
      is contested by the winners of all six continental championships, the current
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
       FIFA World Cup
      </a>
      champions and the country which is hosting the Confederations Cup. This is generally regarded as a warm-up tournament for the upcoming FIFA World Cup and does not carry the same prestige as the World Cup itself. The most prestigious competitions in club football are the respective continental championships, which are generally contested between national champions, for example the
      <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">
       UEFA Champions League
      </a>
      in Europe and the
      <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">
       Copa Libertadores
      </a>
      in South America. The winners of each continental competition contest the
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">
       FIFA Club World Cup
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_competitions">
       Domestic competitions
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_around_the_world" title="Association football around the world">
       Association football around the world
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg/220px-Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg/330px-Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg/440px-Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Auf_Schalke_hosting_Schalke_04_vs_Dortmund_in_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A match in the top football league in Germany
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The governing bodies in each country operate
      <a href="/wiki/League_system" title="League system">
       league systems
      </a>
      in a
      <a href="/wiki/Domestic_association_football_season" title="Domestic association football season">
       domestic season
      </a>
      , normally comprising several
      <a href="/wiki/Division_(sport)" title="Division (sport)">
       divisions
      </a>
      , in which the teams gain points throughout the season depending on results. Teams are placed into
      <a href="/wiki/Table_(information)" title="Table (information)">
       tables
      </a>
      , placing them in order according to points accrued. Most commonly, each team plays every other team in its league at home and away in each season, in a
      <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">
       round-robin tournament
      </a>
      . At the end of a season, the top team is declared the champion. The top few teams may be
      <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">
       promoted
      </a>
      to a higher division, and one or more of the teams finishing at the bottom are
      <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">
       relegated
      </a>
      to a lower division.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The teams finishing at the top of a country's league may be eligible also to play in international club competitions in the following season. The main exceptions to this system occur in some Latin American leagues, which divide football championships into two sections named
      <a href="/wiki/Apertura_and_Clausura" title="Apertura and Clausura">
       Apertura and Clausura
      </a>
      (Spanish for
      <i>
       Opening
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Closing
      </i>
      ), awarding a champion for each.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The majority of countries supplement the league system with one or more "cup" competitions organised on a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_elimination_tournament" title="Single elimination tournament">
       knock-out
      </a>
      basis.
     </p>
     <p>
      Some countries' top divisions feature highly paid star players; in smaller countries and lower divisions, players may be part-timers with a second job, or amateurs. The five top European leagues the
      <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">
       Bundesliga
      </a>
      (Germany),
      <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">
       Premier League
      </a>
      (England),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">
       La Liga
      </a>
      (Spain),
      <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">
       Serie A
      </a>
      (Italy), and
      <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">
       Ligue 1
      </a>
      (France) attract most of the world's best players and each of the leagues has a total wage cost in excess of 600 million/763 million/US$1.185 billion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Variants_and_casual_play">
       Variants and casual play
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Variants_of_association_football" title="Variants of association football">
       Variants of association football
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Street_football" title="Street football">
       Street football
      </a>
     </div>

        To many, soccer is more than just a sport: a video short on the many styles and ethnicities who play football.

     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_Football_Morocco.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1870" data-file-width="2896" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Street_Football_Morocco.jpg/220px-Street_Football_Morocco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Street_Football_Morocco.jpg/330px-Street_Football_Morocco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Street_Football_Morocco.jpg/440px-Street_Football_Morocco.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_Football_Morocco.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Children in
        <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
         Morocco
        </a>
        playing an informal football match in a public space
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Variants of football have been codified for reduced-sized teams (i.e.
      <a href="/wiki/Five-a-side_football" title="Five-a-side football">
       five-a-side football
      </a>
      ) play in non-field environments (i.e.
      <a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">
       beach soccer
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Indoor_soccer" title="Indoor soccer">
       indoor soccer
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">
       futsal
      </a>
      ) and for teams with disabilities (i.e.
      <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_association_football" title="Paralympic association football">
       paralympic association football
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      One of the attractions of association football is that a
      <a href="/wiki/Street_football" title="Street football">
       casual game
      </a>
      can be played with only minimal equipment a basic game can be played on almost any open area of reasonable size with just a ball and items to mark the positions of two sets of goalposts. Such games can often have team sizes that vary considerably from 11-a-side, use a limited and/or modified subset of the official rules, and are likely to be self-officiated by the players.
     </p>

          </a>

          <q>
           Soccer is the most popular sport in the world and is an industry worth over US$400 billion world wide. 80% of this is generated in Europe, though its popularity is growing in the United States. It has been estimated that there were 22 million soccer players in the world in the early 1980s, and that number is increasing. In the United States soccer is now a major sport at both the high school and college levels
          </q>
